<Date>1617535496494</Date><Rating>5< /Rating>< Review>
**GREAT BREAKFAST SPOT IN OLD TORRANCE**

Support the local businesses! Located in Old Torrance, this family-owned caf√© serves a variety of specialty coffee drinks, teas, smoothies, pastries, desserts, and other food items.  We enjoyed a tasty breakfast on their patio -- quaint, friendly, and easy-going. All the good vibes.

PARKING
========
Plenty nearby, on the street or the public lot.

OUTDOOR DINING
================
Several provided patio tables and chairs, completely sanitized and COVID-friendly.
Be sure to order inside first before claiming a spot.

FOOD
=====
ACAI BERRY SMOOTHIE - $6.75
Super fresh and delicious. Didn't taste any added sugar (thank you). Generous portion and I felt much healthier.
RATING: 5/5

BAGEL W/ CREAM CHEESE - $3
What a deal. The bagel's texture was chewy and toasty; the onion flavor was divine. Returning for this one.
RATING: 5/5

SERVICE
=======
Quick, efficient, and friendly. All the likes.
They also accommodated us, 15 minutes after closing (sorry, thank you).
Wonderful staff.

OVERALL
========
Definitely liked the vibe here. Nice caf√© and I'm all for it.

HIGHLY RECOMMEND if you're in town for breakfast. Will order coffee (duh) next time.< /Review>

It's raining all over Southern California so I figured I'd go for a ride.  Lucky for me I can now add to the hundreds of reviews for this charming coffee house in Old Town Torrance!  The Old Torrance Coffee & Tea will not disappoint when you want to getaway but still remain close to home.  Welcomed by a heavy wooden screen door & a beat up pock marked concrete floor I could hardly wait to sit down to watch the rain dancing down from the sky.  The huge picture window here made it worth my while!  Of course they have the standard old scratched up leather chair and couch plus an upholstered chair that's been sat in so often that the springs have sprung.  Trust me though when I tell ya that you won't mind sinking in to it to enjoy your cup of comfort (coffee drinks, tea, chocolate...).< /text>

This was my first visit with my daughter and grandson.  First of all I am a little biased because the manager had a LA Chargers jersey (Woot Woot). The dining area was very clean and presentable. As for the food it was very good. The simple fish and chips was very good and my daughters shrimp and scallops kabob was amazing. What was unique was their tartar sauce which is made fresh daily. Especially for the excellent staff, the atmosphere,  and food.< /text>

<rating>4< /rating>< text>
I didn't really know what to expect. I'm not a big seafood fan. I went on a Friday and they had clam chowder in a sourdough bread bowl. It was really good, I'm a big guy and I couldn't finish the whole thing. Not as good as what I've had at Fishermans wharf in SF, but still good. The clam pieces are small, but there's a good amount. My wife ordered the Basa fillet,  cajun style. It was a really mild and delicious fish. The cajun seasoning did not have a whole lot of flavor to it, but it was really good for someone who does not normally eat fish. I would be happy to return anytime. The place is clean and moderately busy. The wait staff are super nice. We also ordered brownies for dessert. Nothing special about those, I wouldn't get them again. All in all, a really enjoyable dinner.< /text>

<Rate>5<//Rate>< time>
1471199617666<//time>
< text>
Friendly staff, lots of pretty good food for a very reasonable price, pretty ok service. What more can I say? If you're looking for the fanciest, classiest, or best Italian/Americana food in the greater Fresno-Clovis area,  keep looking. But if you want to have a great meal with your family,  or a romantic dinner with a pretty girl, or just a nice place for some lonely drinks Tuesday afternoon, this is it.

I worked at Giuseppe Gallos for a little over a year, and while there were some rough patches, and some times when the food or service was not very great, the restaurant would consistently come back with wonderful, flavourful food and a warm, welcoming atmosphere.

The head chef, Lou, puts so much time and soul into every dish he makes. He works harder than any person I've ever seen, on the food and on the restaurant. He's constantly coming up with new ideas and new ways to be better. When I was a dishwasher, I closed with all of the cooks, and Lou would always stay the longest, cleaning and prepping food for tomorrow. On every holiday, he would work himself to the bone to make sure everything single thing was perfect. He was pretty funny too.

I've seen lots of criticism of the new owners, and a lot of distrust, but when they took over, the restaurant was on its last legs. If you add to that the fact that they didn't have a liquor license for a good four months, it's a miracle they kept the place open. But they did keep it open, and now business is going great (from what I've heard). The new owners have a lot of really great ideas, and even if some of them won't work out,  they will do amazing things for this little Italian restaurant in Clovis.

*Also: Steve makes some hella bomb snacks.</text>

Love Giuseppes, the food tastes homemade which is so comforting, compared to the typical chain restaurant menu. The service is always great, very friendly and accommodating. <name>Shourjya Dasgupta< /name>< review>
Great place to spend the night. It is a first come first serve basis. As soon as you enter the campground, pick up an envelope from the box and look for a empty spot for yourself. Once you occupy your space, fill up the contents in the envelope and put your money in it and drop it in the drop box. It off a total self service campsite.
It had 52 sites to occupy. Each site costs $12 which is pretty reasonable. At max 6 people per site. RVs are not recommended here because the roads are pretty narrow to enter. No potable water in this location.</review>

< Review>
Tamarack flat is a great campground in the high-country of Yosemite national park. It is located towards near Crane Flat about a mile and a half of the SR 120. The campground itself is nicely situated in the bottom of a valley ‚Äî it takes about 10-15 minutes to drive in ‚Äî which keeps a lot of visitors from using it. The campgrounds are nice with bear-vaults, picnic table, fire-pit, parking pad, and your camp-spot. They can, unfortunately, get dirty towards the end of the season. The campground also does not have any running water. All water must be collected from the stream and treated. There is a lot of great hiking right out of the campground which also serves as a trailhead for trails that go up to El Capitan, for example.</Review>

<UserId.>101021102589684358626</UserId.><user_name>Gary Trotta< /user_name><time>1532824440211<//time>< rating>

< Text>
I am the current manager of Bamboo Tree MHP. Management and owners are working diligently to make this park a great and inexpensive place to live. It is an older park and along with that has some "backbone" issues that we are addressing. Just recently we completed a major renovation to part of the sewer system on the RV side of the park and are planning major capital improvements in the coming years. The issues with roaches can only be put on the people that allow them to thrive within their trailers as it is with any home... it is as clean as you make it. We are striving to see that all homes are kept clean and free of any type of infestation. Bamboo Tree is centrally located with a light rail station a five minute walk. Sac Flea Market is right next door with a Rally's a ten minute walk. This is a great park for those on a fixed income with RV rent  averaging $550 a month including elect and water. The mobile home side rent is $474 plus utilities. There is overflow automobile parking available as well as RV and boat storage for a fee. Come on by... it's a nice place with great folks living here... there's a reason we have very little turnover and spaces rent quickly!</Text>

<Text>Bamboo Tree has all the hallmarks of a troubled RV/MH park that has been neglected by management - HOWEVER - There's a new sheriff in town, and the park is under new management, and Kirk and Colleen are great, and are doing a wonderful job removing troublesome tenants. Between May and August 2015, at least 6 of the existing Mobile Homes wound up with new owners.

Sadly, there's not a lot that can be done about the RV side of the park. It's an extremely cramped slab of asphalt wedged in between the Folsom Flea Market and the Social Security Office. There's no shade, and there was no way I'd have been able to deploy my slide with the narrow spaces.

Fortunately, there are a number of spaces available on the Mobile Home side of the park, which are VERY generously sized, reasonably priced, and there is only one available site that has no shade whatsoever.
For a long-term stay, AT&T U-verse is available at up to 18 Mbps as of May 2015.

I stayed 3 months in the summer of 2015, and was VERY happy with my stay.
I'd give the RV side 2 Stars, and the MH side of the park 5 stars, the weighted average being 4 stars.</Text>< GmapID>
